GT Equivalence Verification (BPG9)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 84

Let \(P\) be the only effective variable in the GT (note \(t\) does not appear in the GT), and define the fixed GT function:

\[
\text{GT}(P)=a\Big[(-1+P/\alpha)(1-P/\beta)P+(1-P/\beta)P+(1-e^{-kP})P\Big]
\]
with
\(a=0.1699888096710614\),
\(\alpha=1.0472843670254641\),
\(\beta=10.210545156320043\),
\(k=0.09709294493863778\).

Algebraic simplification:
- The first two bracketed terms share \((1-P/\beta)P\):
\[
(-1+P/\alpha)(1-P/\beta)P+(1-P/\beta)P
=(P/\alpha)(1-P/\beta)P
\]
So
\[
\text{GT}(P)=a\left[\frac{P^2}{\alpha}\left(1-\frac{P}{\beta}\right)+P\left(1-e^{-kP}\right)\right]
\]
Expand polynomial part:
\[
\text{GT}(P)=a\left(\frac{1}{\alpha}P^2-\frac{1}{\alpha\beta}P^3 + P - P e^{-kP}\right)
\]
So GT is exactly:
- a cubic polynomial in \(P\): \(\;A_3P^3+A_2P^2+A_1P\)
- plus one exponential term of the specific form \(-a\,P e^{-kP}\)
- and **no logs, no trig, no rational \(1/(P+\cdot)\), no \(\exp(+kP)\)**, and **no \(t\)-dependence**.

Therefore, any candidate can only match if it can be reduced (by parameter choices) to:
\[
\underbrace{uP^3+vP^2+wP}_{\text{polynomial}} \;+\; \underbrace{z\,P e^{-kP}}_{\text{one exponential term with negative exponent}}
\]
with \(z=-a\) and \(k=0.0970929\ldots\), and with no extra functional forms.

Now check candidates.

---

### 1
Has \(P c0 e^{Pc1}\), logs, Abs, and an extra \(\log(Pc7+1)\) not multiplied by \(P\). Logs cannot be removed unless their coefficients are 0, but then you still have \(P e^{Pc1}\) (wrong sign exponent unless \(c1<0\), but still no way to also create the cubic polynomial unless you add polynomial terms—candidate only has linear-in-\(P\) constants besides logs/exp). Cannot match.

### 2
Contains \(P e^{Pc1}\), \(P e^{Pc4}\), and rational terms \(P*c5/(P*c6+c7)\) and \(c8/(P*c6+c7)\). GT has no rational terms. Setting those to 0 removes them, but then you still have sums of \(P e^{(\cdot)P}\) terms and linear \(P\) only—no \(P^2,P^3\) polynomial. No match.

### 3
Has \(P e^{Pc1}\), \(P e^{Pc4}\), and sinusoidal term \(P^{c5} \sin(\cdot)\). GT has no trig. Kill trig by \(c6=0\), but still lacks cubic polynomial structure. No match.

### 4
Has \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P^{c2} c3 e^{Pc4} + c5\log(\cdot)\). Need no log ⇒ \(c5=0\). Need no \(P^{c2}e^{Pc4}\) unless it becomes \(-aPe^{-kP}\). But it is \(P^{c2}\) times exp; to get \(P e^{-kP}\) need \(c2=1\), \(c4=-k\), \(c3=-a\). Then remaining polynomial is only \(P^2\) and \(P\), but GT also has a \(P^3\) term. No way to create \(P^3\). No match.

### 5
Pure polynomial plus log terms. Set log coefficients \(c5=c7=0\) gives a polynomial with \(P^3,P^2,P\) terms, but GT also has \(-aPe^{-kP}\) exponential term. Candidate has no exponential. No match.

### 6
Has \(P e^{Pc1}\), rational \(P*c2/(Pc3+1)\), and another \(P e^{Pc6}\). GT has no rational; removing it still leaves only exponentials and linear \(P\), no \(P^2,P^3\). No match.

### 7
Polynomial plus logs. Can make polynomial, but no exponential term. No match.

### 8
Has \(P^2\sin(\cdot)\) and exponentials \(P e^{Pc4}, P e^{Pc7}\). Kill sine by \(c0=0\). Still only linear+exponentials, no \(P^2,P^3\) polynomial. No match.

### 9
Sum of \(P e^{(\cdot)P}\) terms plus linear. No \(P^2,P^3\). No match.

Has \(P e^{Pc1}\), \(P e^{Pc4}\), and a sine of an exponential. Cannot reduce to GT. No match.

All terms are rational with common denominator \((Pc1+c2)\), plus exponentials in numerator. GT is not a rational function (it has a standalone exponential term, not divided by linear). No match.

Also entirely over \((Pc1+c2)\). No match.

Uses Max() and \(P^2\cdot\text{Max}\), plus \(P e^{(\cdot)P}\). GT is smooth analytic; Max introduces a kink unless coefficient 0. Setting Max terms to 0 removes them, leaving \(P^3\) + \(P e^{Pc4}\) + linear, but still no \(P^2\). No match.

Has \(P^3\), \(P e^{Pc2}\), linear terms, and log. Kill log. Still no \(P^2\). No match.

Polynomial plus \(\log(c5 e^{Pc6}+1)\). Logs cannot appear in GT. Setting \(c4=0\) removes log, leaving polynomial but no exponential term. No match.

### 20
Has \(P e^{Pc1}\), a power term \(P*c2*(Pc3)^{c4}\), and log. Hard to remove log (set \(c7=0\)). Still has \(P e^{Pc1}\) with positive exponent form (can set \(c1=-k\) to get negative), but polynomial part would be \(P\) plus \(P^{c4+1}\) (from \(P*(P)^{c4}\)). You could set \(c4=2\) to get \(P^3\) and also add linear terms, but you still need a \(P^2\) term as well; candidate has no independent \(P^2\) unless you set \(c4=1\) (gives \(P^2\)) but then no \(P^3\). No match.

### 21
Polynomial \(P^3,P^2\) plus \(P e^{Pc4}\) plus linear. This is structurally close, but the exponential term in GT is \(-a P e^{-kP}\) **and there is no \(+P e^{+kP}\)**. Candidate can set \(c4=-k\) and \(c3=-a\) to match the exponential term, and choose \(c0,c1,c2,c5\) to match polynomial coefficients. However candidate’s polynomial includes **two independent \(P^2\) coefficients** (fine) and a \(P^3\) coefficient (fine) and a linear term (fine). So candidate 21 *can* match exactly:
- set \(c3=-a\), \(c4=-k\)
- set \(c0 = -a/( \alpha\beta)\) (to match \(P^3\) coefficient \( -a/(\alpha\beta)\))
- set \(c1+c2 = a/\alpha\) (to match \(P^2\) coefficient \(a/\alpha\))
- set \(c5 = a\) (to match linear coefficient \(a\))
This yields exactly \(aP - aPe^{-kP} + (a/\alpha)P^2 - (a/(\alpha\beta))P^3\).
So **candidate 21 matches**.

### 22
Has \(P^3,P^2\) and \(P e^{Pc3}\) and \(P\). Missing ability to create both \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) and exponential? It has them, yes: \(P^3 c0 + P^2 c1 + P*c2 e^{Pc3} + P*c4\).
This can also match by setting \(c2=-a\), \(c3=-k\), \(c4=a\), \(c0=-a/(\alpha\beta)\), \(c1=a/\alpha\). **Matches**.

Polynomial plus two \(P e^{Pc6}\) terms and many redundant linear terms. You can combine linear terms and combine exponentials (same exponent). Yes, it has \(P^3\) and \(P^2\) and \(P\). **Matches**.
